The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n     2→//! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n     3→//! we can prove overlap one way or another. On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n     7→//! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n     8→//!\n     9→//! We\n        // check whether the components being borrowed vs\n        // accessed are disjoint (as in the second example,\n        // but not the first).\n        match place_projection_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_c, access_c, bias) {\n            Overlap::Arbitrary => {\n                // We have encountered different fields of potentially\n                // the same union - the borrow now partially overlaps.\n                //\n                // There is no *easy* way of comparing the fields\n                // further on, because they might have different types\n                // (e.g., borrows of `u.a.0` and `u.b.y` where `.0` and\n                // `.y` come from different structs).\n                //\n                // We could try to do some things here - e.g., count\n                // dereferences - but that's probably not a good\n                // idea, at least for now, so just give up and\n                // report a conflict. location-insensitive, but that doesn't work in polonius: locals whose type contains a region\n    // that outlives a free region are not necessarily live everywhere in a flow-sensitive setting,\n    // unlike NLLs.\n    // We do record these regions in the polonius context, since they're used to differentiate\n    // relevant and boring locals, which is a key distinction used later in diagnostics.\n    if typeck.tcx().sess.opts.unstable_opts.polonius.is_next_enabled() {\n        let (_, boring_locals) =\n            compute_relevant_live_locals(typeck.tcx(), &free_regions, typeck.body);\n        typeck.polonius_liveness.as_mut().unwrap().boring_nll_locals =\n            boring_locals.into_iter().collect();\n        free_regions = typeck.universal_regions.universal_regions_iter().collect();\n    }\n    let (relevant_live_locals, boring_locals) =\n        compute_relevant_live_locals(typeck.tcx(), &free_regions, typeck.body);\n\n    trace::trace(typeck, location_map, move_data, relevant_live_locals, boring_locals);\n\n    // Mark regions that should be live where they appear within rvalues or within a call: like\n    // args, regions, and types.\n    record_regular_live_regions(\n        typeck.tcx(),\n        &mut typeck.constraints.liveness_constraints,\n        &typeck.universal_regions,\n        &mut typeck.polonius_liveness,\n        typeck.body,\n    );\n}\n\n// The purpose of `compute_relevant_live_locals` is to define the subset of `Local`\n// variables for which we need to do a liveness computation. We only need\n// to compute whether a variable `X` is live if that variable contains\n// some region `R` in its type where `R` is not known to outlive a free\n// region (i.e., where `R` may be valid for just a subset of the fn body).\nfn compute_relevant_live_locals<'tcx>(\n    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n    free_regions: &FxHashSet<RegionVid>,\n    body: &Body<'tcx>,\n) -> (Vec<Local>, Vec<Local>) {\n    let (boring_locals, relevant_live_locals): (Vec<_>, Vec<_>) =\n        body.local_decls.iter_enumerated().partition_map(|(local, local_decl)| {\n            if tcx.all_free_regions_meet(&local_decl.ty, |r| free_regions.contains(&r.as_var())) {\n                Either::Left(local)\n            } else {\n                Either::Right(local)\n            }\n        });\n\n    debug!(\"{} total variables\", body.local_decls.len());\n    debug!(\"{} variables need liveness\", relevant_live_locals.len());\n    debug!(\"{} regions outlive free regions\", free_regions.len());\n\n    (relevant_live_locals, boring_locals)\n}\n\n/// Computes all regions that are (currently) known to outlive free\n/// regions. For these regions, we do not need to compute\n/// liveness, since the outlives constraints will ensure that they\n/// are live over the whole fn body anyhow.","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":215}}}

The `insert_as_pending_if_two_phase` function (line 341) manages pending two-phase borrow activations by tracking temporary assignments and later uses.\\n\\n## Live Range Calculation\\nLiveness analysis is performed through `type_check/liveness/mod.rs::generate` (line 29) which computes which variables are live at which program points. The core algorithm is in `type_check/liveness/trace.rs::trace` (line 40), which performs a reverse depth-first search through the MIR starting from variable uses and drops, computing USE-LIVE and DROP-LIVE sets for regions in variable types.\\n\\n## Place Conflict Detection\\nPlace overlap analysis is implemented in `places_conflict.rs`.
